PRECAUTIONS\nSevere and Fatal Immune-Mediated Adverse Reactions\nTEVIMBRA is a monoclonal antibody that belongs to a class of drugs that bind to either the programmed death\nreceptor-1 (PD-1) or PD-ligand 1 (PD-L1), blocking the PD-1/PD-L1 pathway, thereby removing inhibition of the\nimmune response, potentially breaking peripheral tolerance and inducing immune-mediated adverse reactions.\nImportant immune-mediated adverse reactions listed under WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS may not include all\npossible severe and fatal immune-mediated reactions.\nImmune-mediated adverse reactions, which may be severe or fatal, can occur in any organ system or tissue.\nImmune-mediated adverse reactions can occur at any time after starting treatment with a PD-1/PD-L1 blocking\nantibody. While immune-mediated adverse reactions usually manifest during treatment with PD-1/PD-L1 blocking\nantibodies, immune-mediated adverse reactions can also manifest after discontinuation of PD-1/PD-L1 blocking\nantibodies.\nEarly identification and management of immune-mediated adverse reactions are essential to ensure safe use of PD-\n1/PD-L1 blocking antibodies. Monitor patients closely for symptoms and signs that may be clinical manifestations\nof underlying immune-mediated adverse reactions. Evaluate liver enzymes, creatinine, and thyroid function at\nbaseline and periodically during treatment. In cases of suspected immune-mediated adverse reactions, initiate\nappropriate workup to exclude alternative etiologies, including infection. Institute medical management promptly,\nincluding specialty consultation as appropriate.\nWithhold or permanently discontinue TEVIMBRA depending on severity [see Dosage and Administration (2.2)]. In\ngeneral, if TEVIMBRA requires interruption or discontinuation, administer systemic corticosteroid therapy (1 to 2\nmg/kg/day prednisone or equivalent) until improvement to Grade 1 or less. Upon improvement to Grade 1 or less,\ninitiate corticosteroid taper and continue to taper over at least 1 month. Consider administration of other systemic\nimmunosuppressants in patients whose immune-mediated adverse reactions are not controlled with corticosteroids.\nToxicity management guidelines for adverse reactions that do not necessarily require systemic steroids (e.g.,\nendocrinopathies and dermatologic reactions) are discussed below.\nImmune-Mediated Pneumonitis\nTEVIMBRA can cause immune-mediated pneumonitis, which can be fatal. In patients treated with other PD-1/PD-\nL1 blocking antibodies, the incidence of pneumonitis is higher in patients who have received prior thoracic\nradiation.\nImmune-mediated pneumonitis occurred in 4.9% (96/1972) of patients receiving TEVIMBRA, including fatal\n(0.1%), Grade 4 (0.3%), Grade 3 (1.6%), and Grade 2 (1.9%) adverse reactions. Pneumonitis led to permanent\ndiscontinuation of TEVIMBRA in 38 (1.9%) patients and withholding of TEVIMBRA in 32 (1.6%) patients.\nSeventy-four (77.1%) of the 96 patients received systemic corticosteroids. Sixty-five (67.7%) of the 96 patients\nreceived high-dose systemic corticosteroids. Immune-mediated pneumonitis resolved in 50% of the 96 patients. Of\nthe 32 patients in whom TEVIMBRA was withheld for pneumonitis, 20 (62.5%) reinitiated TEVIMBRA after\nsymptom improvement; of these, 2 (10%) patients had recurrence of can cause immune-mediated colitis, which can be fatal. Cytomegalovirus infection/reactivation has\nbeen reported in patients with corticosteroid-refractory immune-mediated colitis treated with PD-1/PD-L1 blocking\nantibodies. In cases of corticosteroid-refractory colitis, consider repeating infectious workup to exclude alternative\netiologies.\nImmune-mediated colitis occurred in 0.8% (16/1972) of patients receiving TEVIMBRA, including Grade 3 (0.3%)\nand Grade 2 (0.4%) adverse reactions. Colitis led to permanent discontinuation of TEVIMBRA in 4 (0.2%) patients\nand withholding of TEVIMBRA in 5 (0.3%) patients. Twelve (75%) of the 16 patients received systemic\ncorticosteroids. Eight (50%) of the 16 patients received high-dose systemic corticosteroids. Two (12.5%) of the 16\npatients received immunosuppressive treatment. Immune-mediated colitis resolved in 93.8% of the 16 patients. All 5\npatients in whom TEVIMBRA was withheld for colitis reinitiated TEVIMBRA after symptom improvement; of\nthese, none of the patients had recurrence of colitis.\nImmune-Mediated Hepatitis\nTEVIMBRA can cause immune-mediated hepatitis, which can be fatal.\nImmune-mediated hepatitis occurred in 1.2% (24/1972) of patients receiving TEVIMBRA, including fatal (0.1%),\nGrade 4 (0.2%), Grade 3 (0.5%), and Grade 2 (0.4%) adverse reactions. Immune-mediated hepatitis led to\npermanent discontinuation in 3 (0.2%) patients and withholding of TEVIMBRA in 13 (0.7%) patients. Eighteen\n(75%) of the 24 patients received systemic corticosteroids. Thirteen (54.2%) of the 24 patients received high-dose\nsystemic corticosteroids. Two (8.3%) of the 24 patients received immunosuppressive treatment. Immune-mediated\nhepatitis resolved in 70.8% of the 24 patients. Of the 13 patients in whom TEVIMBRA was withheld for hepatitis, 7\n(53.8%) reinitiated TEVIMBRA after symptom improvement; of these, none of the patients had recurrence of\nhepatitis.\nImmune-Mediated Endocrinopathies\nAdrenal Insufficiency\nTEVIMBRA can cause immune-mediated adrenal insufficiency. For Grade 2 or higher adrenal insufficiency, initiate\nsymptomatic treatment, including hormone replacement as clinically indicated. Withhold TEVIMBRA depending on\nseverity [see Dosage and Administration (2.2)].\nImmune-mediated adrenal insufficiency occurred in 0.4% (8/1972) of patients receiving TEVIMBRA, including\nGrade 4 (0.1%), Grade 3 (0.1%), and Grade 2 (0.3%) adverse reactions. Adrenal insufficiency did not lead to\npermanent discontinuation of TEVIMBRA. TEVIMBRA was withheld in 7 out of 8 patients. All 8 patients received\nsystemic corticosteroids. Three (37.5%) of the 8 patients received high-dose systemic corticosteroids. Adrenal\ninsufficiency resolved in 25% of the 8 patients. Of the 7 patients in whom TEVIMBRA was withheld for adrenal\ninsufficiency, 5 (71.4%) reinitiated TEVIMBRA after symptom improvement; of these, none of the patients had\nrecurrence of adrenal insufficiency.\nHypophysitis\nTEVIMBRA can cause immune-mediated hypophysitis. Hypophysitis can present with acute symptoms associated\nwith mass effect such as headache, photophobia, or visual field defects. Hypophysitis can cause hypopituitarism.\nInitiate hormone replacement as clinically indicated. Withhold or permanently discontinue TEVIMBRA depending\non severity [see Dosage and Administration (2.2)].\nHypophysitis/hypopituitarism occurred in 0.2% (4/1972) of patients receiving TEVIMBRA, including Grade 2\n(0.2%) adverse reactions. Hypophysitis did not lead to permanent discontinuation in any patient, while treatment\nwas withheld in 1 (0.1%) patient. Three (75%) of the 4 patients received systemic corticosteroids. One (25%) of the\n4 patients received high-dose systemic corticosteroids. Hypophysitis/hypopituitarism did not resolve in the 4\npatients. For the 1 patient where TEVIMBRA was withheld for hypophysitis/hypopituitarism, there was no\nrecurrence of hypophysitis/hypopituitarism.\nThyroid Disorders\nTEVIMBRA can cause immune-mediated thyroid disorders. Thyroiditis can present with or without endocrinopathy.\nHypothyroidism can follow hyperthyroidism. Initiate hormone replacement for hypothyroidism or institute medical\nmanagement of hyperthyroidism as clinically indicated. Withhold or permanently discontinue TEVIMBRA\ndepending on severity [see Dosage and Administration (2.2)]."},"context":{"uri":"gs://mlr_upload/pi.pdf","pageNumber":6}}]}
